2 If they ((ºÀjÃ±ÀégÀ, gÁWÀªÁAPÀ, PÉgÉAiÀÄ ¥ÀzÀägÀ¸À) wrote in the reign of Narasimha I (1141-1173), they must belong to about that time (1165); but then they could scarcely have received their inspiration from Basava, and their works must be evidence of a general revival of Saivism, of which Basava's work was only a part. * "The Urubhanga, which has erroneously been treated as a tragedy, is on the contrary the depicting of the deplorable fate of an enemy of Krishna…. The Urubhanga's conclusion is happy, not tragic, for the worshipper of Krishna". – Keith's Sanskrit Drama. p. 38

** 1-2-1955

2 The Vedic data show that only the eldest son had the right to marry and inherit all the property. Modern kinship terms and certain kinship usages confirm this conjecture. The younger brothers were allowed access to the wife or wives of the eldest brother, and if a younger brother married, he sinned against his brother – A.B.O.R.I. *"The mereoric rise of Hyder from a comman soldier to the head of a powerful and orderly state has a parallel in the rise of napoleon the other great foe of the English duyring the sexcond half of the eighteenth century. The dynasty of Hyderwas to use the words of a distinguished writter napoleonic in the suddenness of its rise, the brilliancy of its success and the completeness of the overthrow...... His son Tippu had not the masterful resources throne founded by genius was lost by the recklessness of a vain successor." An Account of the compaign of Mysore (1799), by Sir Alexander Allen. page117.

1. The History of the reign of Tipu Sultan being a Continuation of the neshani Hydari written by Mir Hussein Persian Manuscript . . . bye Col. W. Miles (1864.

2.* The History of Hyder Shah (alias Hyder Ali Bahadur) and an abridged account of the life of his son Tipu Sultan (First edition 1784) by M.M.D.L.T.

3. An account of the Campaign in Mysore (1799) by Sir Alexander allan.

4. Buchanan's Travels (1807, 1870)

5. Stewarts Descriptive Catalogue of the oriental library of Late Tippu Sultan of Mysore (to which are prefixed memoris of Hyder Ali Khan and his son Tipu Sultan).

6. Select letters of Tippu Sultan, arranged and transalted by william Kirkpatrick (1811)

7. The life of Hyder Ali by Francis Robson (1786).

8. Hyder Ali and Tippu Sultan by L.B>Bowring (Rulers of Indian Series).

9. Memoris of Tippu Sultan – bye an officer in the East Indian Service (1819).

10. A review of the Origin Progress and Result of the decisive war with the late Tippu Sultan in Mysore-bye James Salmond (london 1800).

11. A Revies of the origin and conduct of the war with tippu Sultan – bye Alexander Beatson.

12. Narrative of the campaign in India reminationg with war with Tippu Sultan in 1792 – bey Majot Dirom.

13. Wilks History of Mysore. 2 Vols (1810)

14. Mysore Gazetter.
